              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26262267-lindsey-dahling?shelf=lindsey-marti-book-club">lindsey-marti-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3221576529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14341099781794870419"><b>We need more Slytherin narrators in the world.</b><br/><br/><br/>I’ve always found myself drawn to characters with Slytherin traits. They’re much more interesting than your purely good characters (sorry, Jon Snow). This book’s narrator, Alessandra, is a rare one. Legitimately. I’ve NEVER seen a narrator like this who wasn’t the villain. <br/>She’s confident. <br/>She’s unapologetic. <br/>She’s cunning. <br/>She’s observant. <br/>She’s direct. <br/><br/>I didn’t spend one second of this book internally screaming, “COME ON. JUST ASK HIM WHAT HE REALL</span>
  <span id="freeText14341099781794870419" style="display:none"><b>We need more Slytherin narrators in the world.</b><br /><br /><br />I’ve always found myself drawn to characters with Slytherin traits. They’re much more interesting than your purely good characters (sorry, Jon Snow). This book’s narrator, Alessandra, is a rare one. Legitimately. I’ve NEVER seen a narrator like this who wasn’t the villain. <br />She’s confident. <br />She’s unapologetic. <br />She’s cunning. <br />She’s observant. <br />She’s direct. <br /><br />I didn’t spend one second of this book internally screaming, “COME ON. JUST ASK HIM WHAT HE REALLY MEANS. JUST TELL HIM HOW YOU FEEL. ASK HIM TO CLARIFY” because homegirl Alessandra just goes for it. She’s well aware she’s not an angel and never pretends otherwise. <br /><br />Mad respect.<br /><br />She legit tells you on page 1 that she killed someone when she was 15. Is she sorry? ABSOLUTELY NOT. <br /><br />Again, mad respect.<br /><br />She doesn’t need protecting. <br />She doesn’t need saving. <br />Just get the fuck out of her way because she’s got this.<br /><br />👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻👏🏻<br /><br />The only thing I’m mad about in regards to this book is I spent the entire time reading thinking it was the first book in a series and I would get to spend more time with these characters. But noooooooo. I just had to be illiterate and/or misremember. What a moron.<br /><br /><br />One final note—I fully support the pro-women, anti-slut shaming stance this book takes. It absolute annihilates that whole idea that “beautiful virgin female MC” is the only way to go. Because, get the smelling salts, Alessandra sleeps with men FOR FUN. BECAUSE SHE LIKES IT. She doesn’t have feelings for them. She just likes to bang. AND THAT’S OKAY. 💕 Her friend in the book IS a beautiful virgin and IS waiting until marriage—AND THAT IS ALSO OKAY! 💕 <br /><br />Just look:<br /><br /><blockquote>“I’m not a trollop...I’m a sexually empowered woman, and there is nothing wrong with that.” </blockquote><br /><br />YAAAASSSSSSSS!<br /><br />AND THEN:<br /><br /><blockquote>“There is nothing silly about waiting until you want to. Don’t let anyone ever tell you otherwise. It is your body to do with as you will... Waiting. Not waiting. One lover. A hundred lovers. There should be no judgment either way. A woman is not defined by what she does or doesn’t do in the bedroom.”</blockquote><br /><br />I legit thought my heart was going to burst and I was just going to die right there in my sweatpants-and-Christmas-sweatshirt-quarantine-look because THANK. YOU. <br /><br />STOP THE SLUT SHAMING.<br /><br />STOP THE SLYTHERIN SHAMING.<br /><br />And goddammit, if you don’t know what a Slytherin is, please go read Harry Potter.<br /><br />Otherwise I, a Gryffindor, will have to charge after you and beat you over the head with it (Gryffindors are not subtle) (see: this entire review).</span>

<div id="review_3252165950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3252165950" />
    <a title="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16276747-ashleigh-a-frolic-through-fiction"><img alt="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600437893p2/16276747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3252165950?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" href="/user/show/16276747-ashleigh-a-frolic-through-fiction">Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250761231" href="/book/show/51974936-the-shadows-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16276747-ashleigh-a-frolic-through-fiction?shelf=physically-own">physically-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3252165950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1360152936737293422">I am...so sad. Marketed as a Slytherin romance with a leading lady who is unapologetically cunning, I was all for this book. It was one of my anticipated releases, but it ultimately just fell short for me.<br/><br/>First thing I noted was the simplicity of the writing. Not every book has to be elaborately written, but when the plot is quite literally being laid out on a plate in front of you with zero room for doubt or interpretation, there's no space left for guessing or intrigue. You're just told everyt</span>
  <span id="freeText1360152936737293422" style="display:none">I am...so sad. Marketed as a Slytherin romance with a leading lady who is unapologetically cunning, I was all for this book. It was one of my anticipated releases, but it ultimately just fell short for me.<br /><br />First thing I noted was the simplicity of the writing. Not every book has to be elaborately written, but when the plot is quite literally being laid out on a plate in front of you with zero room for doubt or interpretation, there's no space left for guessing or intrigue. You're just told everything, and move on with a simple "oh ok". What's more, I didn't really understand the need to almost obsessively describe the clothing. It seemed the author wanted to portray a sense of decadence in the court (understandably) and show the main character as having an interest in clothing, but the book just mentioned clothing <i>constantly</i>. Yes it can make a statement, but there were so many scenes of the main character designing dresses...when nothing really came of it? She simply became a trendsetter, moving on. Apart from we didn't move on, because not once could her legs be mentioned without it specifying she's wearing pants. <i>"he touched my pant-clad leg"/"my pant-clad legs"</i> and details to that effect were mentioned again and again, even when her outfit was literally just mentioned and there was no need for further reiteration. A petty thing to point out, but it just seemed to drive you towards a belief that her clothing will be central to the plot somehow when it just...wasn't, really.<br /><br />The characters themselves I just didn't believe. Our leading lady walks about claiming she's dangerous and not one to cross, but it didn't really feel that way. Especially not when within the space of a page, she arrives at a new place and immediately makes friends with the first people who talk to her, claiming something along the lines of "well I'll need friends". That may be the case, but it isn't that easy and there was certainly no sign of that friendship growing at all. They were just claimed and that was that. The uneasiness supposedly surrounding the Shadow King didn't feel legit. The threat surrounding him didn't feel dangerous at all. The main's father and sister were just awful for no good reason, her father's reasonings behind the attempts to pull her away from the court just didn't make sense. There was a random Robin-Hood sideline story that popped up out of nowhere?? I am just...confused. So very confused at what this story was trying to do. <br /><br />And the final straw, so to speak, was the plot twist. It was ridiculous. It made no sense. Literally didn't understand how that could happen and the reasoning behind it was so unsubstantial I just blinked. I don't want to sound this harsh but I just...no. I couldn't do it.<br /><br />Sadly this book just flopped for me, in every way possible. I know many people enjoy it and for what it's worth, I will say it's a quick and easy read. Probably nice if you want something fun but kind of dark? But unfortunately it's a no from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1360152936737293422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3119734435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10530774975888829286">4/30/2020<br/><br/>3.5 stars Perfect for those new to fantasy and wanting to enter into the genre. And also great for the avid fantasy reader who, like me, often needs a break from investing into heavy, 600 page minimum, 4-8 installment high fantasy series. <br/><br/><i>The Shadows Between Us</i> is called a <b>
  <i>”Slytherin Romance”</i>
</b> by the author herself and that enough is exactly what any of us Harry Potter fans want. Especially those in House Slytherin, and those who have spent countless hours reading very naughty Draco,</span>
  <span id="freeText10530774975888829286" style="display:none">4/30/2020<br><br>3.5 stars Perfect for those new to fantasy and wanting to enter into the genre. And also great for the avid fantasy reader who, like me, often needs a break from investing into heavy, 600 page minimum, 4-8 installment high fantasy series. <br><br><i>The Shadows Between Us</i> is called a <b>
  <i>”Slytherin Romance”</i>
</b> by the author herself and that enough is exactly what any of us Harry Potter fans want. Especially those in House Slytherin, and those who have spent countless hours reading very naughty Draco, Snape, and even Tom Riddle fanfiction (hey, this is a safe place, right?) <br><br><b>BUT!</b> Unfortunately, this doesn’t deliver in the way of <i>dark, evil, villainous, antihero, naughty shenanigans</i> as I had so pleadingly, desperately hoped...<br><br>....and instead <b>it’s more of a light fantasy with some serious fluff</b> that us bad girls just aren’t vibing. <br><br>But (and here’s another but), not-bad-enough-for-me disappointment aside, this is still entertaining. And even better, it’s only 326 pages long. And a stand alone! <b>A, quick, easy read, with some really fun steamy bits (did it get hot in here or—) that I really appreciated, And a nice cast of characters.</b><br><br>Speaking of characters, If anything at all, read this just for Alessandra, the MC, <b>who is one of the only YA characters extremely comfortable with her sexuality!</b><br><br>Let’s have a moment of appreciation for a <b>Non-Virginal YA Character</b> *general applause* <br><br>I was thrilled to find in only the first chapter, and also the characters introduction, that she was a bit of a—*cough*—<i>
  <b>THOT</b>
</i>....wait! I’m not slut-shaming, I just lack the vocabulary for a woman who thoroughly, and unabashedly, enjoys sex...<br><br><i>
  <b>”I’m not a trollop,” I announce to the empty room. “I’m a sexually empowered woman, and there is nothing wrong with that.”</b>
</i><br><br>I love this! Are you loving this or am I just weird? I feel seen! Finally I can relate! <br><br>The word trollop is thrown around very mildly (from only Alessandra’s father and sister, I believe) but that’s about it as far as shaming goes. Even the <i>Shadow King</i> himself does not see virginity as a virtue of treasure or requirement in considering of a courtship, <br><br><i>”Are you a virgin?” I ask. <br><br>...he seems beyond amused by the question. “No. Are you?”<br><br>“Would it matter if I wasn’t?” I dare ask. <br><br>“Not at all,” he says immediately.</i> <br><br>I really enjoyed this aspect of Alessandra’s character. It is refreshing in this genre to skip past all the first times, and cherishing virginity stuff, especially in whatever era this supposedly takes place in, and being presented to a king as a noble woman and certain expectations are of utmost importance. <br><br>Speaking of <i>era</i>....it is entirely unclear to me because, as many have said before me this lacks almost heavily in world building. I knew that going in, and I didn’t mind, I was looking for a lighter fantasy and mostly wanted the romance. But I can admit that the lack of world building, despite my preference over less details, did begin to make an impact on my enjoyment. <br><br>But it was easy for me to ignore and sit sit back and have fun. <br><br>I wish <i>The Shadows Between Us</i> would’ve been something more sinister and gothic but I can always find that elsewhere and not have bitterness in my disappointment as I was still entertained. <br><br><br><br><br>3/15/20 <br>Okay *heavy breathing*, I heard <i>Slytherin Romance</i> and I don’t even care if the world building is sub-par, I need I need I need 🐍 <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586992944ra/29299387.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>1/3/2020 <br>Oh my gothic heart, this cover</span>

<div id="review_3220351836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3220351836" />
    <a title="Andrea Ashwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51797495-andrea-ashwood"><img alt="Andrea Ashwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574398207p2/51797495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3220351836?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Ashwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Ashwood" href="/user/show/51797495-andrea-ashwood">Andrea Ashwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250761231" href="/book/show/51974936-the-shadows-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51797495-andrea-ashwood?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51797495-andrea-ashwood?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3220351836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5873094631108803478"><b>[English Review - Reseña en Español]</b><br/><br/><b> |English|</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557641335ra/27492304.gif' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>“The point is, Father, I know what I’m doing. And I’m going to keep doing whatever I wish, because I am the master of myself. And you? You’re going to send me to the palace with the next wave of women to see the king, because if there’s anything I’m good at, it’s getting men to propose to me.”<br/>Father’s eyes narrow. “How long have you been planning this?”<br/>“Years.”</blockquote>(You will find my synopsis below)<br/>This is one of those stories that you know won't forget in</span>
  <span id="freeText5873094631108803478" style="display:none"><b>[English Review - Reseña en Español]</b><br><br><b> |English|</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557641335ra/27492304.gif" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>“The point is, Father, I know what I’m doing. And I’m going to keep doing whatever I wish, because I am the master of myself. And you? You’re going to send me to the palace with the next wave of women to see the king, because if there’s anything I’m good at, it’s getting men to propose to me.”<br>Father’s eyes narrow. “How long have you been planning this?”<br>“Years.”</blockquote>(You will find my synopsis below)<br>This is one of those stories that you know won't forget in a long time.<br>It will be a book that I’ll never tire of recommending.<br>And it’s a standalone, which is like...<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588204537ra/29379199.gif" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Can someone explain me which part of the brain must be stimulated to create the fabulous protagonist that Tricia has produced? I constantly do sudokus.<br><br>First I will introduce you to her, and then you’ll know what I’m talking about:<br><u>Alessandra:</u> <br>The vile protagonist.<br>Boastful and cruel. Creative and strategist. Brave and sexy.<br>Vengeful. Fierce. Leader.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588204537ra/29379200.gif" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>You'll love her.<blockquote>“They've never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. And they never will.”</blockquote>The fact that, for the time in which it’s set (although it’s fantasy), Alessandra is proud of her sexuality has dazzled me. I adore that there will be many people who read this book and there’s the least possibility of moralizing about the normality of the topic.<blockquote>“I’m a sexually empowered woman, and there is nothing wrong with that.”</blockquote>Alessandra will face the prejudices of society as she knows, with indifference. <br>She knows what many people think about what a woman should or shouldn’t do, always listen and be silent. But she wasn’t born to be silenced.<br>Many of her enemies will underestimate her along the way, as they believe that a "woman like her" cannot harbor any intelligence.<blockquote>“The poets say a virtuous woman’s worth is above rubies [...]”<br>The poets can say whatever they damned like. A woman’s worth is not decided by what’s between her legs but by what is in her mind.</blockquote>The maturity that the characters acquire throughout the events is incredible.<blockquote>“I just need a moment to gather my courage”<br>(He) nods in understanding.<br>“Doing the right thing is not always easy. And being the bigger person, the first to reach out with kindness, takes great strength of character. You needn’t fear, though, Alessandra. Doing the right thing is never the wrong answer.”</blockquote>Of course what has most intrigued me about the story was the romance, a relationship that goes gradually and is disclosed in detail. <blockquote>“All the time in the world is worth nothing if I don't get to spend it with you.”</blockquote>Kallias, The Shadow King, is incalculable and Alessandra will do everything in her power to conquer him and become queen, but she never imagined meeting someone so similar to her.<blockquote>“But it’s practically an unspoken law that ladies must be virgins on their wedding nights.”<br>“It’s no law of mine. In fact, I’ve made a point of doing my best to give ladies the same rights as men. [...] And besides, how can men expect all the ladies to remain virgins while they don’t? The numbers don’t add up.”</blockquote>(By the way, it might be me, but I saw sexual tension everywhere.)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588767918ra/29425608.gif" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But.<br>What has made me have so much affection for the book and put it in my ranking of favorites has been the friendship.<br>I’ve rarely had the opportunity to read such a beautiful and pure friendship between women.<br>And I know that this sounds peculiar and unpleasant, but it’s a fact that, both, in real life and in literature, friendship between women is often impossible, since there is competition toxicity that I don’t understand. We see this topic of "hate" everywhere.<br>I’ve adored them. The scenes starring all three always placed a smile on my face. They’re made for each other. Tricia, provides scenes between them with important and awareness talks.<blockquote>“There is nothing silly about waiting until you want to. Don’t let anyone ever tell you otherwise. Is it your body to do with as you will.”<br>She smiles at me then, and I worry that I might be the first person to tell her that.<br>Waiting. Not waiting. One lover. A hundred lovers. There should be no judgement either way. A woman is not defined by what she does or doesn’t do in the bedroom.</blockquote>Their friendship causes favorable changes in themselves, and that has made me fall in love. The moments of humor, inspiration and motivation have marked this book for me.<blockquote>(Situation: (One of them) wants her friend to stop emulating her in everything to get love)<br>“Do you know how I was able to catch (his) attention?”<br>She shakes her head.<br>“By being myself. By discussing what I wished to discuss and behaving how I wished to behave and wearing what I wished to wear. It is not conforming to a standard that drew (his) attention. If you wish to make a happy match, I think you should do the same. Don’t be afraid of who you are. Say what you wish. Be who you wish. Don’t try to be someone else. You don’t need to catch a man who wants me. You want to catch a man who wants you.”</blockquote>A wonder, isn’t it?<br>So, finally, what’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35702241.The_Shadows_Between_Us" title="The Shadows Between Us by Tricia Levenseller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadows Between Us</a> about?<br><br><b>Alessandra</b> has been waiting for a long time the power and attention she deserves once and for all.<br>Her sister, a spoiled fool who has the same intellectual capacity as a toucan, is the only one her father loves. Instead, for him Alessandra is a commodity before his eyes, he only sees in her the power and fortune he can obtain when he promises it to any man who is willing to bid for her hand.<br>Alessandra's feelings disappeared long ago, when she fell in love for the first and only man who broke her heart.<br>Never again, she promised herself.<br>Since then, she turned indifference and passion into her armor. Her weapon? The secrets. Those who pass through her bed, fill her with secrets that she will use to her advantage.<br>Her self-confidence attracts her prey, and until now, no one who has been in her sights has denied her. For that reason she has devised a plan.<br>Tired of not being respected, she only sees one option. The only one that will make no one give her orders, ignore her or dare betray her.<br>Become the queen.<br>The Shadow King is looking for a wife. She will become his temptation. And when he proclaim her the queen, she will kill the king and be the total sovereign of the kingdom.<br>After all, power resides in the crown, and Alessandra is thirsty for it.<br><br><b>Kallias</b>, The Shadow King, has been waiting for a long time the freedom and control that his title demands by law. But he still has a few months to reach the required age and finally exercise the position he wants.<br>Master his kingdom. Conquer new territories. Change the laws. Do as he pleases, without having to rely on advice.<br>His heart has hardened from the worst betrayals.<br>Kallias wants revenge on those who ruined his life, but every time he seems to find a clue he finds only mirages.<br>And a new rebellion rises up against the king...<br><br><b>Alessandra and Kallias</b> have their hopes on each other.<br>For her, the priority is to get the crown, even if to obtain it she must protect the king from those who want to end his life. At least, until he makes her his queen and then she kills him herself.<br>The enemies won’t be the only impediment in the challenge to obtain the throne. <br>Kallias is distant. <br>Feelings are a weakness that he doesn't want to experience.<br>But Alessandra won’t see the cold heart of The Shadow King as an obstacle but as a challenge that she will win.<br><br>Nothing is what it seems.<br>Between the palace walls truth it’s hidden behind false smiles and promises of loyalty.<br><br><b> |Español|</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533796947ra/26099898.gif" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>"La cuestión es, padre, que sé lo que estoy haciendo. Y voy a seguir haciendo lo que desee, porque soy la dueña de mí misma. ¿Y tú? Me enviarás a palacio con la próxima oleada de mujeres para ver al rey, porque si hay algo en lo que soy buena, es en conseguir que los hombres se me declaren."<br>Los ojos de padre se estrechan."¿Cuánto tiempo llevas planeando esto?<br>"Años."</blockquote>(Encontraréis mi sinopsis más abajo)<br>Esta es una de esas historias que sabes que no vas a olvidar en mucho tiempo.<br>Será un libro que nunca me cansaré de recomendar.<br>Además es autoconclusivo, o sea, increíble.<br><br>Por cierto, ¿alguien me puede explicar qué parte del cerebro hay que estimular para crear la fabulosa protagonista que Tricia ha inventado?<br>Para que me entendáis:<br><u>Alessandra:</u> <br>La vil protagonista. <br>Alardeante y cruel. Creativa y estratega. Valiente y sexy. <br>Vengativa. Feroz. Líder.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588643735ra/29416448.gif" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>La vais a amar.<blockquote>“Nunca encontraron el cuerpo del primer y único hombre que me rompió el corazón. Y nunca lo harán."</blockquote>El hecho de que, para la época en la que se inspira (aunque sea fantasía), Alessandra se enorgullezca de su sexualidad me ha encandilado. <br>Adoro que vayan a haber muchos jóvenes que lean este libro y exista la mínima posibilidad de moralizar sobre la normalidad del tema.<blockquote>"Soy una mujer sexualmente empoderada, y no hay nada de malo en ello."</blockquote>Alessandra se enfrentará contra los prejuicios de la sociedad como ella sabe, con indiferencia. Muchos de sus enemigos la subestimarán, ya que creen que una “mujer como ella” no puede albergar inteligencia.<blockquote>"Los poetas dicen que el valor de una mujer pura está por encima de los rubíes [...]"<br>Los poetas pueden decir lo que quieran. El valor de una mujer no se decide por lo que hay entre sus piernas, sino por lo que está en su mente.</blockquote>Ole, ole y ole.<br>Es increíble la madurez que van adquiriendo los personajes a lo largo de la historia.<blockquote>"Solo necesito un momento para reunir coraje."<br>(Él) asiente en señal de comprensión.<br>“Hacer lo correcto no siempre es fácil. Y ser una gran persona, la primera en arribar con amabilidad, requiere una gran entereza. Sin embargo, no debes temer, Alessandra. Hacer lo correcto nunca es la respuesta incorrecta."</blockquote>Lo que más me ha intrigado del libro era el romance. Una relación que fluye poco a poco. <br>Kallias, el Rey de las Sombras, y Alessandra nunca imaginaron conocer a alguien tan semejante a ellos.<blockquote>"Pero es prácticamente una ley tácita que las mujeres deben ser vírgenes en su noche de bodas."<br>"No es una de mis leyes. En realidad, he hecho todo lo posible para darles a las mujeres los mismos derechos que a los hombres. [...] Además, ¿cómo pueden los hombres esperar que todas las mujeres sigan siendo vírgenes mientras ellos no lo hacen? No tiene sentido."</blockquote>(Por cierto, puede ser que sea yo, pero veía tensión sexual por todas partes.)<br>Lo que me ha hecho cogerle tanto cariño al libro y meterlo en mi ranking de favoritos ha sido la amistad.<br>Las escenas que protagonizan las tres siempre colocaban una sonrisa en mi rostro. <br>Están hechas las unas para las otras. Su amistad provoca cambios favorables en ellas mismas, y eso me ha enamorado. Los momentos de humor, de inspiración y de motivación, han marcado, para mí, este libro.<blockquote>“No hay nada de absurdo en esperar hasta que quieras. No dejes que nadie te diga lo contrario. Eres tú quien debe hacer lo que quiera con su cuerpo."<br>Entonces me sonríe y temo que pueda haber sido la primera persona en decírselo.<br>Esperar. No esperar. Un amante. Cien. No debería haber juicio de ninguna manera. Una mujer no se define por lo que hace o no en el dormitorio.</blockquote>Una maravilla, ¿verdad?<br><br>Mi sinopsis (sin spoilers) del libro:<br><br><b>Alessandra</b> lleva mucho tiempo anhelando el poder y la atención que se merece de una vez por todas.<br>Su hermana, una estúpida mimada, es la única a quien su padre ama. En cambio, para él, Alessandra es una mercancía ante sus ojos. Solo ve en ella el poder y fortuna que podrá obtener cuando la prometa a cualquier hombre que esté dispuesto a pujar por su mano.<br><br>Los sentimientos de Alessandra desaparecieron tiempo atrás, cuando se enamoró por primera y única vez, y le rompieron el corazón.<br>Desde entonces convirtió la indiferencia y la pasión en su armadura. ¿Su arma? Los secretos. Aquellos que pasan por su cama la colman de secretos que ella utilizará a su favor.<br>Su seguridad en sí misma atrae a sus presas, y hasta ahora nadie que haya estado en su punto de mira se le ha negado. Por esa razón ha ideado un plan.<br>Cansada de no ser respetada, solo ve una opción.<br>Convertirse en la reina. <br>El Rey de las Sombras busca esposa. Ella será su tentación. Y cuando la proclamen reina, matará al rey y será la total soberana del reino. <br>Al fin y al cabo, el poder reside en la corona, y Alessandra está sedienta de ella.<br><br><b>Kallias</b>, el Rey de las Sombras, lleva mucho tiempo anhelando la libertad y el control que demanda su título por ley. Pero todavía le quedan unos meses para cumplir la edad requerida y ejercer por fin el cargo que tanto desea. <br>Dominar su reino. Conquistar nuevos territorios. Cambiar las leyes. Hacer lo que le plazca, sin tener que depender del consejo.<br>Su corazón se ha endurecido a causa de las peores traiciones. <br>Kallias está deseoso de ejercer venganza sobre aquellos que arruinaron su vida, pero cada vez que parece encontrar una pista solo halla espejismos, y una nueva rebelión se alza en contra del rey.<br><br><b>Alessandra y Kallias</b> albergan sus esperanzas el uno en el otro.<br>Para ella su prioridad es conseguir la corona, incluso si para obtenerla debe proteger al rey de aquellos que quieren acabar con su vida, al menos hasta que la haga su reina y ella misma le mate.<br>Los impíos no serán el único impedimento en el desafío por obtener el trono, ya que Kallias se muestra distante. Los sentimientos son una debilidad que él no quiere experimentar.<br>Pero Alessandra no verá el frío corazón del Rey de las Sombras como un obstáculo, sino como un reto que está dispuesta a ganar.<br><br>Nada es lo que parece.<br>Entre los muros de palacio la verdad está oculta tras sonrisas falsas y promesas de lealtad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5873094631108803478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2918828300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11500687353229097946">3.5 starts, <b>and I feel so conflicted!</b><br/>After much consideration, I feel the book is closer to three stars than four. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587652033ra/29343675.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>Normally I like the fact that Tricia Levenseller's books are quite short (330 ish pages), because to me it means that no matter how stressful my life is at the time of starting the book, I will still be able to finish it in a reasonable amount of time. The problems with reading short books, and standalone novels, is that I always end up wanting more. More world-building. More ba</span>
  <span id="freeText11500687353229097946" style="display:none">3.5 starts, <b>and I feel so conflicted!</b><br>After much consideration, I feel the book is closer to three stars than four. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587652033ra/29343675.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Normally I like the fact that Tricia Levenseller's books are quite short (330 ish pages), because to me it means that no matter how stressful my life is at the time of starting the book, I will still be able to finish it in a reasonable amount of time. The problems with reading short books, and standalone novels, is that I always end up wanting more. More world-building. More background story. More character development. More tension. More everything! The Shadows Between Us is no exception, and I think this is one of those stories with characters that would have done really well as a series. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"They’ve never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. And they never will.<br>I buried Hektor Galanis in a hole so deep, even the devils of the earth couldn’t reach him."</i>
</blockquote><br>Tricia Levenseller really knows how to start of a book! Her writing is fluent and fast paced, making this a quick read. She also has an affinity for creating strong female characters, not perfect or flawless in any way, which is why I love them. Her main characters are always unapologetic when it comes to their desires (like power, fortune etc), and her books are normally set in a time where (like in modern days to be fair) men are often considered more valued than women. <s> So it's extra satisfactory to read when the women kick their asses.</s><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587652168ra/29343685.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>"Waiting. Not waiting. One lover. A hundred lovers. There should be no judgment either way. A woman is not defined by what she does or doesn’t do in the bedroom."</i>
</blockquote><br>If I'm being really honest, I hated the "perfectly wrapped up ending", because I was hoping for a final twist, or something that would make this book stick with me after putting it down. I also really disliked the final part of the book, due to several reasons that would be spoilery to write down <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like how she just forget the poison she hid in her room... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3394515877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3394515877" />
    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3394515877?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2020</a>

<div id="review_3318212497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318212497" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34465556-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588296669p2/34465556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318212497?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/34465556-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=pub-2020">pub-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318212497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17039691167688739580">Just based on the blurb, I was feeling some Rhysand vibes and was pretty excited from that alone. Oh, how wrong I was. Kallias wasn’t completely disappointing, but he was far more Kaz Brekker than Rhysand. Still, I’m not convinced he was as good as either. <br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 2.5</b><br/><br/>This is described as a slytherin romance, which I was hoping would make my slytherin heart happy. Alas, I didn’t particularly like Alessandra or Kallias. I suppose this is because we have different goals in life and thus a di</span>
  <span id="freeText17039691167688739580" style="display:none">Just based on the blurb, I was feeling some Rhysand vibes and was pretty excited from that alone. Oh, how wrong I was. Kallias wasn’t completely disappointing, but he was far more Kaz Brekker than Rhysand. Still, I’m not convinced he was as good as either. <br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 2.5</b><br /><br />This is described as a slytherin romance, which I was hoping would make my slytherin heart happy. Alas, I didn’t particularly like Alessandra or Kallias. I suppose this is because we have different goals in life and thus a different code to follow, but their lack of morals and constant selfishness didn’t help to endear me to the pair. <br /><br />I will say that Alessandra is quite different from most YA protagonists. You know the type—she only wants a simple life, and she doesn’t know why all of these things seem to be happening to her. Alessandra is a schemer. She takes what she wants. She is calculating, and I appreciated the fact that she didn’t seem as naive as YA protagonists typically are. <br /><br />My main problem with this is the way she and Kallias think about the peasants that Kallias rules over. For example, there’s a Robin Hood character that they seek to capture. They are both obsessed with conquering new kingdoms to rule over. They like to order public floggings or hangings to stifle revolts. It screams of classism. <br /><br />Going back to Alessandra, I will say that I think she was incredibly stupid at times. For someone who was portrayed as being so cunning and conniving, she put her plan of marrying the king at risk on multiple occasions. When she sneaks out to a boxing match with Leandros, she decides to tell everyone to call her the “Shadow Queen,” a direct play on Kallias’ title. How is she so certain that there are no other nobles or palace servants in the crowd? How is she so certain that no one will recognize her? Her only excuse in this case is her drunkenness. In this world, a lady’s virginity is very important for marriage, but Alessandra tells several people that she barely knows about her previous lovers. Now, I know Alessandra supports women’s rights, but she doesn’t receive any push back from anyone for this, despite the fact that word is sure to spread to Kallias’ advisors. It seems super unrealistic, or Alessandra is incredibly lucky in both cases. <br /><br />Speaking of Alessandra’s feminism, I was initially worried that this might be a repeat of Graceling and it’s psuedo-feminism, but I was reasonably satisfied since Alessandra has two female friends and a feminine hobby. However, Alessandra’s friendship with them just kind of happens without any effort on Alessandra’s part. It’s far too convenient. Then, when they do become friends, all they talk about it balls, boys, and clothes. We don’t get to know much—if anything—about their families, other friends, hobbies, or anything about them, really. <br /><br />The plot itself moved pretty quickly. I was actually wondering where the book would go next halfway through because it had gone so fast that I wasn’t sure how there was so much book left. Unfortunately, I found some of the plot twists to be extremely predictable. Coming from me, that’s a big deal. I never see <i>anything</i> coming. So long as an author puts some sort of effort into a plot twist, I’ll be shocked 95% of the time. In this particular novel, I was only shocked maybe 60% of the time. <br /><br />More than that, the romance just didn’t really do it for me. Other than a few gushy moments with Kallias that I liked, the entire book failed to elicit any sort of emotion from me. Luckily, I did find it interesting enough to keep reading nearly constantly. It’s also been applauded as enemies to lovers, but I don’t feel like that’s an accurate representation of the romance since they never actually hate each other. Despite the fact that Alessandra is planning to kill Kallias, she’s doing it for her own gain and not because she dislikes him. On Kallias’ side, it’s more of a friends to lovers situation. Altogether, it was underwhelming. <br /><br />Overall, the book was mostly pleasant and enjoyable. However, the story is in no way remarkable. If a slytherin romance sounds like your cup of tea, give it a read. If not, you won’t be missing out on much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17039691167688739580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3232085942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3232085942" />
    <a title="Hillary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary"><img alt="Hillary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601752862p2/18999155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3232085942?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hillary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hillary" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary">Hillary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/44670142-the-shadows-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232085942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6467473748261337788">2.5 stars<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>There’s something about watching him give orders that has my blood flowing faster in my veins. He has such power. Men are forced to obey him without a word of protest. They would do anything he commanded.<br/>I want that power.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>It’s the worst when the first half of a book gives you a lot of expectations for what is currently happening and what’s to come, and then those expectations aren’t met, so you feel like you’ve been scammed a little.</b><br/><br/>I’m not saying I didn’t have fun reading this book</span>
  <span id="freeText6467473748261337788" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>There’s something about watching him give orders that has my blood flowing faster in my veins. He has such power. Men are forced to obey him without a word of protest. They would do anything he commanded.<br />I want that power.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>It’s the worst when the first half of a book gives you a lot of expectations for what is currently happening and what’s to come, and then those expectations aren’t met, so you feel like you’ve been scammed a little.</b><br /><br />I’m not saying I didn’t have fun reading this book, but for sure it was disappointing. Even if I felt kind of the same about this author’s debut, so I don’t really know why I expected to like this one more than <i>Daughter of the Pirate King</i>. <br /><br />It was the slytherin thing that convinced me, and at the beginning it did feel like the book was going to deliver on that front, except Alessandra started doing stupid thing after stupid thing. Plus, I realized there would be no plot except for the romance, which wasn’t that great in the first place. <b>The lack of world building or of a major plot made it impossible for me to really fall for the story.</b> I wanted scheming and ambition, but this only had episodic-like court intrigue that I didn’t care about and a lackluster mystery I didn’t bat an eyelash at. There were more tedious descriptions of the clothes everyone is wearing every day than plot, just saying. Sorry not sorry 🤷🏻‍♀️<br /><br />In the end, yes, I enjoyed this, but it’s no masterpiece. It’s a fun read and it’s a page-turner, but it didn’t change my life. <b>This is a good book if you want some fast and entertaining fantasy that doesn’t need too much brain power to get through it.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6467473748261337788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3024577833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3024577833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5462170314912283713"><i>They never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. <br/>And they never will.</i> <br/><br/>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/>In life we learn a lot of lessons. <br/>We learn that life isn’t always fair. <br/>Never perfect. <br/>Life isn’t easy either, no one will give you anything for free. <br/>You have to work for it. <br/>And when Alessandra gave her heart to a boy, she wanted to have his heart back. <br/>But instead, he broke it. He tore it apart.<br/>So she killed him. <br/>With her broken heart she swore to herself to never love again.<br/>She swore to t</span>
  <span id="freeText5462170314912283713" style="display:none"><i>They never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. <br>And they never will.</i> <br><br>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>In life we learn a lot of lessons. <br>We learn that life isn’t always fair. <br>Never perfect. <br>Life isn’t easy either, no one will give you anything for free. <br>You have to work for it. <br>And when Alessandra gave her heart to a boy, she wanted to have his heart back. <br>But instead, he broke it. He tore it apart.<br>So she killed him. <br>With her broken heart she swore to herself to never love again.<br>She swore to take what she wanted with everything she has. <br>And now she has her eyes one so someone special. Or rather something. <br>A throne. A kingdom. Power. <br>But to get what she wants she needs to conquer the heart of the most powerful man in her kingdom. <br>Every girl wants to get their hands on him. <br>Marry the king, be a queen. <br>But Alessandra isn’t every girl. <br>She doesn’t want to marry the king, be the queen on his side. <br>No, she wants to rule alone. <br>As a queen without a king. <br><br>Oh, I loved this so much. I had so much fun reading this book and it helped me out of a reading slump. <br>Definitely one of my favorites now. <br><br>Character 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Alessandra is a strong minded girl who knows what she wants. <br>She reminded me a little bit of Jude from cruel prince. But this girl is a little bit different, where Jude is talented with a knife and sword, Alessandra has an amazing talent with a needle. She know how to create a look from head to toe and do this nearly completely alone. <br>She know how to get people to fall in love with her. Even the king. <br>Next to being a cold stone bitch she is also extremely funny and knows her worth. <br><br><i>”But i could weigh in. Help you. You’re not the only one who wants you to succeed.” <br>I Pause at the top of the steps. <br>“Have you ever seduced a man before?” <br>Fathers cheeks redden. “Of course not!” <br>“Then I don’t see why I should need you to weigh in on anything. Rest assured father, if there’s any way in which you could prove useful, I will tell you. For now, I can handle things.”</i><br><br>Now look at the male counterpart of our amazing main girl. His name is shadow king and that’s what he is literally made of sometimes. Shadows. How cool is that? <br>Maybe you’re thinking - is this his name? <br><i>Shadow King</i>? <br>No, his name is actually Kallias and he is literally the perfect dark broody Love interest. <br>Next to this he was also a really intelligent, intriguing and powerful king.<br>But instead of being a total sexist (like literally nearly every other male character in this book) he was a strong feminist. <br>He would’ve changed a lot of rules if he could, but his young age forced him to rely and rule through a council. <br>He treated women with respect and knew how to agree to better ideas. That was mu absolute favorite character treat. <br><br>All in all I loved all of the characters. But especially my darling Alessandra. <br>She was a queen. <br><br>World 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><i>They say the shadow king has some sort of power, but no one knows what it is. <br>Some say he can command the shadows to do his bidding, that he can use them to kill - choke the life out of his enemies. <br>Others say they’re a shield. <br>That no blade can pierce his skin. <br>And even others say that the shadows speak to him, whispering the thoughts of those all around. <br>I certainly hope that last one isn’t true.</i> <br><br>There isn’t much magic in this world, save the shadow king and his shadow magic. <br>He seems to be made of shadows and as long as no one touches him, he is nearly as powerful as a god. He can be translucent like a ghost, so now one can touch him and because of that power the king can life until a hundred years, if he wants to. <br>But the power can be taken away from him. <br>By a touch or by having a child. <br>Oh, how dangerous it can be to fall in love. <br><br>Relationships 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>A few years back I always thought I’m house slytherin. But after doing many tests I realized - Jessi you’re not a slytherin your a ravenclaw. <br>And you know? Now I’m a proud ravenclaw. <br>But you know who is a perfect slytherin? <br>Killias and Alessandra. <br>Those two were so perfect for each other. <br>They had a wonderful relationship - they were supportive, strong minded, but also knew how to accept a better idea. They were intelligent and cruel if they needed to. <br>And the most important of all: they flirted like little teenagers. Their banter was wonderful. <br>I smiled all the way down this book. <br>Absolutely love this. <br><br>Writing style 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>The writing was wonderful. Fast paced, entertaining and sometimes even funny. <br>The author showed us sexist problems and that there are people who realize that and want to change the world. <br>Like I said, I was in a terrible reading slump, until this book came along the way. <br>It caught my eye a while ago, because the description literally screamed at me “this is a book for you, READ IT!” <br>And then it was the happy day and I was so excited. Finally! 🥳🥳🥳<br><br><br>________________________________________________<br><br>Me, reading the description: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571994036ra/28348252.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I WANT IT NOW!</span>

<div id="review_2825665801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="ʙᴇʟʟᴀ.: ☾**:.☆*.:｡." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206809"><img alt="ʙᴇʟʟᴀ.: ☾**:.☆*.:｡." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549201639p2/5206809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2825665801?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ʙᴇʟʟᴀ.: ☾**:.☆*.:｡." class="user" itemprop="url" name="ʙᴇʟʟᴀ.: ☾**:.☆*.:｡." href="/user/show/5206809">ʙᴇʟʟᴀ.: ☾**:.☆*.:｡.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2825665801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14544016343868907406">I loved Warrior of the Wild from the author. I liked it so much that I set my expectations too high for this one. Unfortunately, my expectations were not met, and maybe this is just another case of "it's me not you".<br/>There were too many inconsistencies for me to be able to fully enjoy this book. While in WotW I loved the writing, in this one the writing always felt too abrupt. I enjoyed the first 40% of the book and from then on just lost interest. <br/>So without further delay, <br/>What I enjoyed:<br/>- Aless</span>
  <span id="freeText14544016343868907406" style="display:none">I loved Warrior of the Wild from the author. I liked it so much that I set my expectations too high for this one. Unfortunately, my expectations were not met, and maybe this is just another case of "it's me not you".<br />There were too many inconsistencies for me to be able to fully enjoy this book. While in WotW I loved the writing, in this one the writing always felt too abrupt. I enjoyed the first 40% of the book and from then on just lost interest. <br />So without further delay, <br />What I enjoyed:<br />- Alessandra's ambitions. It was over the top but still awesome to read about it.<br />- Allessandra's sense of humor. She was great at internal jokes and banter with people. <br />- Alessandra's love and dedication to making her own dresses and outfits. She was an amazing designer and I felt so incredibly happy to see a female character working in something she actually likes. I was hoping till the end that she would acknowledge her talent and creativity and make her profession as a Royal Tailor. <br />- Female Friendships that I enjoyed a lot.<br />- Allessandra's confident sexuality.<br />- Female empowerment. <br />- Demodocus the dog. I mean I LOVE when YA books present a character with a pet. <br />What I did not like:<br />- Alessandra forgot her initial purpose to kill the king too quickly. There was not even much internal conflict.<br />- She <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[killed her first boyfriend because he broke up with her. Her lack of impulse control and villainous actions were not consistent with the personality she shows after she moves out of her house. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-Alessandra becomes someone completely out of character that reminds nothing of the villain she was supposed to be. She was presented as a remorseless villain at first and then turns into a special snowflake that does not really much wrong and that every male in the book seems to succumb to insta-love for her. <br />- The villain was so predictable I saw it coming miles away. <br />- Too many convenient encounters, balls, letters and walks and then we have a very rushed, fast-paced ending.<br />- Kallias lacked depth and there was nothing different in him from the typical trope of lonely brooding dark hero with a tragic past that I've already read 1000 times in YA. <br />- I did not get why Alessandra hated her sister so much that she wished for her death when her sister did nothing to deserve such intense hate. To me, her sister was just another victim of their father.<br />- The worldbuilding could have been more detailed. I got vibes from a medieval Italian-esque world but not enough to make it unforgettable. <br /><br />So overall, I liked the first 40% and then I just lost interest and it took me months to finish it. It's an enjoyable book but I still think, considering the premise, it could have had the potential to become so, so much more. <br />Anyway, because I loved Warrior of the Wild, I'll be looking forward to reading what the author writes next:)<br /><br /><br />ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review (Thank you!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14544016343868907406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2079529503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2079529503" />
    <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy"><img alt="Cindy ✩☽♔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605643833p2/3222333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy ✩☽♔" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy">Cindy ✩☽♔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=otps-feels">otps-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2079529503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8966636592836906489"><b>“They've never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. And they never will.”</b><br/><br/>Truly the Slytherin romance we were all promised. <br/><br/>Our heroine is beautiful, cunning, charming and manipulative. Our hero is, well, shadowy, handsome, smart and calculating. They are truly birds of a feather. <br/><br/>Be forewarned, if you're looking for a tale in which the protagonists use their wicked minds to create a country that is better for all, please, look somewhere else. These two are in no way for t</span>
  <span id="freeText8966636592836906489" style="display:none"><b>“They've never found the body of the first and only boy who broke my heart. And they never will.”</b><br /><br />Truly the Slytherin romance we were all promised. <br /><br />Our heroine is beautiful, cunning, charming and manipulative. Our hero is, well, shadowy, handsome, smart and calculating. They are truly birds of a feather. <br /><br />Be forewarned, if you're looking for a tale in which the protagonists use their wicked minds to create a country that is better for all, please, look somewhere else. These two are in no way for the people. They are conquerors. They want power. They want control. And they want each other. <br /><br />This book was not perfect, but it was highly addicting. I never wanted to put it down. So why, you might ask, not round up to five stars? <br /><br />Two reasons. <br /><br />One: As much as I adored Kallias aka the Shadow King. He did at times feel lacking in depth. This is why, as I mentioned in one of my status updates, this book would have benefited greatly from dual POV. We see inside Alessandra's mind, we know she's Slytherin at her core. But we do not get that same understanding of Kallias, which I why, between the two, I liked him less. One of the most compelling aspects of reading about anti-heroes/heroines is seeing how their mind works. Understanding what makes them tick. We are robbed of that with Kallias in this book. <br /><br />Two: The ending. <br />It was abrupt. It felt out of place with the rest of the book. After everything that happened, I wanted to see our queen claiming her rightful place on the throne beside her king. We got no grand, triumphant return. No theatrics or pageantry, it was a shame and completely unbefitting of Alessandra's character. <br /><br />Alas, no book is perfect obviously. But I can say this one pleasant change from the usual YA fare, where I am constantly expected to root for the occasionally naive, often over-trusting, good guys. So cheers to that. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8966636592836906489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mLByCBWtKrWe35OtK6RaOPfwU9v/3UMtyRZ8BisV9miH6OzzOC6GI846JkAl1swxjh12CKJp6AcYb2GIw0rABg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
